\"F0EDE8\", type: ShadingType.CLEAR },\n    children: [new TextRun({ text: t, font: \"Courier New\", size: 21, bold: true, color: C.darkBlue })] });\n}\n\nfunction mh(name, color) {\n  return new Paragraph({ spacing: { before: 360, after: 120 },\n    border: { bottom: { style: BorderStyle.SINGLE, size: 6, color, space: 8 } },\n    children: [\n      new TextRun({ text: \"\\u25A0 \", color, 0);\n  return new Table({\n    width: { size: tw, type: WidthType.DXA }, columnWidths: colWidths,\n    rows: [\n      new TableRow({ children: headers.map((h, i) => new TableCell({\n        borders, C.warmGray : C.white, type: ShadingType.CLEAR }, margins: cm,\n        children: [new Paragraph({ children: [new TextRun({ text: cell, size: 19, font: \"Arial\" })] })],\n      })) })),\n    ],\n  });\n}\n\nconst hdr = new Header({ children: [new Paragraph({\n  border: { bottom: { style: BorderStyle.SINGLE, size: 1, color: C.lightGray, space: 4 } },\n  children: [\n    new TextRun({ text: true, color: C.teal }));\n    if (i < steps.length - 1) runs.push(new TextRun({ text: \"  \\u2192  \", font: \"Arial\", size: 20, color: C.accent }));\n  });\n  return new Paragraph({ spacing: { before: 120, after: 120 }, alignment: AlignmentType.CENTER,\n    shading: { fill: \"F8F6F3\", type: ShadingType.CLEAR }, children: runs });\n}\n\nfunction labeled(label, color, items) {\n  return [\n    new Paragraph({ spacing: { before: 240, after: 80 },\n      border: { left: { style: BorderStyle.SINGLE, size: 12, color, space: 8 } },\n      indent: { left: 200 },\n      children: [new TextRun({ text: label, font: \"Arial\", size: 20, bold: true, color })] }),\n    ...items.map(c => new Paragraph({ spacing: { after: 120 }, indent: { left: 400 },\n      children: [new TextRun({ text: c, font: \"Arial\", size: 20, color: C.black })] })),\n  ];\n}\n\nfunction math(t) {\n  return new Paragraph({ spacing: { before: 100, after: 100 }, alignment: AlignmentType.CENTER,\n    shading: { fill: \"F0EDE8\", type: ShadingType.CLEAR },\n    children: [new TextRun({ text: t, font: \"Courier New\", size: 21, bold: true, color: C.darkBlue })] });\n}\n\nfunction mh(name, color) {\n  return new Paragraph({ spacing: { before: 360, after: 120 },\n    border: { bottom: { style: BorderStyle.SINGLE, size: 6, color, space: 8 } },\n    children: [\n      new TextRun({ text: \"\\u25A0 \", color, size: 24 }),\n      new TextRun({ text: name, font: \"Arial\", size: 26, bold: true, color }),\n    ] });\n}\n\nfunction tbl(headers, rows, colWidths) {\n  const tw = colWidths.reduce((a, b) => a + b, 0);\n  return new Table({\n    width: { size: tw, type: WidthType.DXA }, columnWidths: colWidths,\n    rows: [\n      new TableRow({ children: headers.map((h, i) => new TableCell({\n        borders, bold: true, color: C.white, size: 20, font: \"Arial\" })] })],\n      })) }),\n      ...rows.map((row, ri) => new TableRow({ children: row.map((cell, ci) => new TableCell({\n        borders, width: { size: colWidths[ci], type: WidthType.DXA },\n        shading: { fill: ri % 2 === 0 ? C.warmGray : C.white, type: ShadingType.CLEAR }, margins: cm,\n        children: [new Paragraph({ children: [new TextRun({ text: cell, size: 19, font: \"Arial\" })] })],\n      })) })),\n    ],\n  });\n}\n\nconst hdr = new Header({ children: [new Paragraph({\n  border: { bottom: { style: BorderStyle.SINGLE, size: 1, color: C.lightGray, space: 4 } },\n  children: [\n    new TextRun({ text: The outer parts experience the highest velocity (v = 2\u03c0Rf) and thus the highest stress. If we make the outer layers lighter (lower density), the stress at the outer edge drops dramatically.\n\nThis is exactly the principle used in:\n- Flywheel energy storage (lighter rim materials)\n- Turbine blade design (hollow tips)\n- The Earth itself (dense core, lighter mantle/crust)\n\nFor a torus, if we use dense materials at the center (close to the axis of rotation) and progressively lighter materials toward the outer edge, the stress distribution becomes much more favorable.\n \nThe hoop stress at any radius depends on integrating the density and radius outward\u2014if density decreases with radius, that integral shrinks, which means lower stress and the ability to push higher speeds. With an optimal gradient where density falls off as 1/r\u00b2, the stress becomes uniform throughout the structure, which is the ideal scenario. This would theoretically let us increase the surface velocity by a factor of \u221a2 or more compared to a uniform density torus.\n\nWith this density gradient applied to a thin ring, I can achieve roughly 2-3\u00d7 improvement in maximum velocity, which means either 2-3\u00d7 larger radius at the same rotation rate or 4-9\u00d7 more surface area.
